  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_803963bf-6e38-4698-89dc-2abb49cdb724'
      });
    }

I do feel bad for Massie, because it’s really not obvious to anyone but herself, and maybe Claire, how hard she actually works to keep her friends on top, but I know they’ll all get back together. <br/><br/>It was also weird though how little of Claire there was in this story.   <span id="freeText2399965493315296376" style="display:none">Everyone is finally starting to grow up and branch out! I do feel bad for Massie, because it’s really not obvious to anyone but herself, and maybe Claire, how hard she actually works to keep her friends on top, but I know they’ll all get back together. <br /><br />It was also weird though how little of Claire there was in this story. I think she maybe had like, 15 lines of dialogue. It focused mostly on Kristen and Dylan, which was new and fresh, so I didn’t mind, but I hate that the books really only focus on 2 or 3 girls at a time, when there’s 5 in the group. <br /><br />Claire, though! What a good friend. Honestly. I’m glad that Massie is finally seeing that. I get the whole loyalty thing, too, because I’m the same way, but it’s nice to see that she’s definitely maturing. </span>

<div id="review_54168451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54168451" />
    <a title="Jacqueline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1806012-jacqueline"><img alt="Jacqueline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576550159p2/1806012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54168451?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline" href="/user/show/1806012-jacqueline">Jacqueline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jacqueline by: </span>
      Davishay Lawrence in 7th grade :)
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer54168451&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54168451" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5640381432186600987">Being a Claire and Cam fan, I didn't like how the main character (typically Claire) had changed to the evil ruler, Massie. I have a hate/love relationship with how she figures out her own evil personality, decides to do something about it, but then decides that if the world doesn't like it, they could just be on their own. This would be a great moral, but Massie is one of those girls I would never speak to, due to her incredible rudeness, especially to her own friends. <br/><br/>I'm really happy though th</span>
  <span id="freeText5640381432186600987" style="display:none">Being a Claire and Cam fan, I didn't like how the main character (typically Claire) had changed to the evil ruler, Massie. I have a hate/love relationship with how she figures out her own evil personality, decides to do something about it, but then decides that if the world doesn't like it, they could just be on their own. This would be a great moral, but Massie is one of those girls I would never speak to, due to her incredible rudeness, especially to her own friends. <br /><br />I'm really happy though that Dylan gets a guy, who suits her perfectly. Too bad Massie can't get over that it's her ex, but I guess, we can't all win our wars.<br /><br />It's about darn time that Alicia pulls away from Massie. Let someone with some sort of brains be the leader if there is to be a leader of a particular group or middle school girls.<br /><br />Kristen's boy problems are pretty sad. That's all I can say about that.<br /><br />I'm just surprised by the fact that Claire and Cam went to Massies pool party. It shows Claires character, which I value the most out of just about anybody else in The Clique series.<br /><br />I find these books super addicting, can't help but admit it, but at the same time I hate the very basis of it. The Clique series is my personal placebo to drama, because I try to pull myself away from that as much as possible now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5640381432186600987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11158886575167399415">Probably in almost every school there’s always a group of people who may be better known amongst the students of their school or in other words popular. At Briarwood-Octavian Country Day School, the Pretty Committee would be that group of people. Massie Block, Kristen Gregory, Dylan Marvil, Alicia Rivera, and Claire Lyons who’ve always stayed on top even when there were obstacles, so what will happen when Alicia decides that she wants to be the leader of the Pretty Committee and not Massie? Or w</span>
  <span id="freeText11158886575167399415" style="display:none">Probably in almost every school there’s always a group of people who may be better known amongst the students of their school or in other words popular. At Briarwood-Octavian Country Day School, the Pretty Committee would be that group of people. Massie Block, Kristen Gregory, Dylan Marvil, Alicia Rivera, and Claire Lyons who’ve always stayed on top even when there were obstacles, so what will happen when Alicia decides that she wants to be the leader of the Pretty Committee and not Massie? Or when Dylan has a crush on someone she’s not suppose to, one of the Pretty Committee’s ex-boyfriend? Or also when Kirsten has to choose between her two best friends? Oh and what will happen to Massie the Pretty Committee’s alpha as she and Claire watch the Pretty Committee fall apart? This is P.S. I Loathe You, a Clique novel by Lisi Harrison, the #1 New York Times bestselling series.<br />	I found this to be the best book of the entire Clique series. It’s entertaining, full of drama and thrilling. There are a lot of things in the book that a reader would be able to connect to. Like liking someone but not sure weather or not they like you back. Or having to choose between two things and knowing that choosing one thing would probably hurt the other. Throughout the book, it has made me laughed and relate to each of the characters. <br />	I would recommend this book to teens that enjoy books about friendship and romance. Once you begin reading this book, it’ll keep you flipping the pages till you’ve completely finished the entire 208 pages of the book. Read P.S. I Loathe You by Lisi Harrison whenever you get he chance, you won’t regret it. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15468503597560600349"><br/><br/> PS. I Loath You, is the tenth book of the clique series. Unlike other books dealing with pointless and tacky comebacks and climbing their social status, this time the plot is more realistic and had grabbed my attention. The character named Massie has been the leader of the clique for long period of time but happens if her friends are of sick of it? As she enjoys controlling others, she abuses her power. She uses her friends just to steal the spotlight in cheerleading and to stop them to not sur</span>
  <span id="freeText15468503597560600349" style="display:none"><br /><br /> PS. I Loath You, is the tenth book of the clique series. Unlike other books dealing with pointless and tacky comebacks and climbing their social status, this time the plot is more realistic and had grabbed my attention. The character named Massie has been the leader of the clique for long period of time but happens if her friends are of sick of it? As she enjoys controlling others, she abuses her power. She uses her friends just to steal the spotlight in cheerleading and to stop them to not surpass her. Soon her guilt was eating her, she looks back on her action on what horrible things she had done to her friends, but is it too late to apologize? Later on Kristen, Alica, and Dylan has chosen their separate paths and thinking their leader was a burden. Leaving Massie with her true friend, Claire.<br /><br /> This is one of the books I enjoyed cause every page kept me excited even if the reading level is below mine, I still thought it was great how the author did something new by turning the main characters against each other. Also how it gave a message to the readers that no matter how much you enjoy/like something and when you indulge it you soon regret doing it.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7335057170352318470">The Pretty Committee has officially ended its boy-fast, and Massie Block is crushing her way into Dempsey Solomon's heart.   <span id="freeText7335057170352318470" style="display:none">The Pretty Committee has officially ended its boy-fast, and Massie Block is crushing her way into Dempsey Solomon's heart. What she has to do urgently is make her ex jealous. Just to make matters worse, one of Massie's BFFs starts crushing on Derrington, (Derrick Herrington) her ex. And she also finds out that LBR (Loser Beyond Repair) Layne Abeley, is crushing on that same guy. Things start getting really messed up while the PC is lovesick. So, to make sure that she is the one that wins Dempsey's heart, she start BOCD's first ever cheerleading squad. She does this just because Derrington's injured and Dempsey's going out to substitute his goalie spot. Will she win Dempsey's heart with the cheerleading squad, or will the Pretty Committee fall apart before she even gets a chance?<br /><br />I liked this book because it shows what kind os sacrifices friends have to do for each other. Sometimes, other stuff gets in the way. It shows what a true alpha (Massie Block) does to gain confidence when something happens. The book has some tender moments and some feelings of dislike; sort of like the title. All the PC wants is to have a soul mate and a close place in the Pretty Committee, without hurting anyone's feeling's.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer164371305&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer164371305" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4960688739564346139">First of all this book is extremely suspenseful. Second of all, when you start reading it you won't stop until you fall asleep; which is not going to happen because you'll never get bored with this one. This was the second the clique book that I read, and it was better times ten than Charmed and Dangerous. <br/> This book was so helpful to me since what happened to Kristen happened to me when I was reading this book. My friends love me so much but they hate each other and each one wants me with her. </span>
  <span id="freeText4960688739564346139" style="display:none">First of all this book is extremely suspenseful. Second of all, when you start reading it you won't stop until you fall asleep; which is not going to happen because you'll never get bored with this one. This was the second the clique book that I read, and it was better times ten than Charmed and Dangerous. <br /> This book was so helpful to me since what happened to Kristen happened to me when I was reading this book. My friends love me so much but they hate each other and each one wants me with her. So I kept on doing what Kristen kept on doing: avoiding them. The problem is that whatever Kristen wasn't going to work with my friends at all. <br />There was this last part, when Kristen talked to Dempsey for Massie and Layne, that made me scream literally because I didn't expect it at all. It was like you're running away from a bomb and then BOOM! It just hit me.<br /><br />	Again I recommend this book for everyone because I bet that everybody will like and ah-dore it. And by the way, be alert from that part because if it made me scream I don't know what it will do to you! <br /></span>

<div id="review_1798280454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1798280454" />
    <a title="Tiffany Spencer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52552606-tiffany-spencer"><img alt="Tiffany Spencer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519342160p2/52552606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1798280454?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany Spencer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany Spencer" href="/user/show/52552606-tiffany-spencer">Tiffany Spencer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798280454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17231202894687794291">P.S I Loathe You<br/>PLOT: Massie is losing her iron-tight grip on The Clique. Dylan and Derrington (whose real name we find out is Derrick) start to fall for one another when discovering they have the same taste after getting sent to detention over a prank. Even though Massie is long since over Derrington won't release him from her grip because she hasn't secured her new crush and thus allowing no one to go after Derick. Claire after the events of the boy fast is now all over Cam all the time. Alici</span>
  <span id="freeText17231202894687794291" style="display:none">P.S I Loathe You<br />PLOT: Massie is losing her iron-tight grip on The Clique. Dylan and Derrington (whose real name we find out is Derrick) start to fall for one another when discovering they have the same taste after getting sent to detention over a prank. Even though Massie is long since over Derrington won't release him from her grip because she hasn't secured her new crush and thus allowing no one to go after Derick. Claire after the events of the boy fast is now all over Cam all the time. Alicia tho clearly the best dancer of the group is pushed to second in charge when Massie starts a group of cheerleaders called the Socc HERS. And Kristen with the biggest storyline's loyalty is torn between helping her BFF Clique friend (Massie) and her BFF Witty Committee friend (Layne) acquire the love of Dempsey. Especially when she herself has feelings for Dempsey and has a boyfriend of her own Duane whose home from the island he left for to model.<br /><br />My THOUGHTS:<br />This book was VERY satisfying because even though the title describes perfectly my feelings for Massie (PS I LOATHE YOU) and really this series, it should be called the downfall of Massie. Let's review this bitch's insanity. She's so controlling she "physically" puts her claim on Derrick by spraying him with her perfume. She's so self-absorbed that she thinks HE needs to get over HER when Dylan had it right in thinking you need to get over yourself. Even though Kristen is one of her supposed "BFFs" and Clique members she looks down her snotty little noise about where she lives until she needs her to try to get next to Dempsey. Then she has the audacity to make keys to all their houses and private spaces like it's her right. Wouldn't the parents have something to say about this CHILD having a key to their houses? This (wanting to curse here) brat is a user plain and simple. Her moods switch up with the wind. She gets mad at Kristen for not stopping Layne from moving in on her "territory". Then at the beginning spouts this bs poem she made up about how they won't let anything get in the way of their friendship again and how they'll be there for each other 24-7. She picks and chooses when to be there for them, but if they aren't there for her 24-7 she gets mad and turns to the closest one she thinks is still loyal. Which they all do whatever they want behind her back and lie to her face. Then has the nerve to wonder what she's done wrong and try to justify her foul behavior because she rationalizes it's what they need. Which sounds like an abusive husband who beats his wife because he thinks she needs to be kept in line. Two of the greatest moments in the book came when Dempsey calls her "assey" and tells her that Layne is a better friend to Kristen than she'll ever be, and when Dylan reads her like a book and walks out of the PCC. None of the member's but Claire show up and leaves her there stood up and looking crazy. Claire is described in this at one point in always doing what she wants regardless and I thought to myself SINCE WHEN? Claire is more stuck up Massie's behind than the rest of the Clique. As we see she's the only one that stays. I was proud of Dylan in PS I LOATHE YOU, but slightly annoyed with her because while she's not as over the top ridiculous as Massie, but I am SO over her obsessing book after book about her weight. Chick, please! In this book, she even wonders if Derrick thinks a MANNEQUIN looks better than her! A MANAQUINN! I think the only time I really agreed with Massie was about Claire who didn't even exist in this book but the end. The rest she was in some kind of sappy, love, haze that I could have done without reading. That leaves Alicia and Kristen. Alicia and Dylan seemed to have discord in this book. Not that that's news for these backstabbing clique of phonies, but I can't remember from the last book why this was so it came off as a hunh? You would think after reading in the boy fast book that shows Alicia sneaking around with Josh she'd not be so quick to rat Dylan out. Or was Dylan the one that ratted her out? I don't care enough to go back and look that up so moving on. Kristen was the only one I gave a damn about in this. Why? Once upon a time, a LONG time ago I found myself in her shoes: dating one guy and realizing I was in love with someone else. It did NOT end well AT ALL! But I have a feeling that (well maybe I'm hoping) that to further add to the Queen B's fall Kristen will end up with Dempsey. Of course, this will cause strife with Massie AND Layne. But I'm not sure I liked Layne in this book. What is it about Layne's that turn out to be self-righteous bitches in books (BSC)? And I wondered why after the way Massie's treated Kristen (in this book alone) was she so upset and felt she owed Masie anything. I hope this series ends with them all leaving Massie. That would so be worth the time I invested.<br /><br />RATING: 10. Just alone for how Massie gets read AND dumped in the end. If there were emoji's I'd put several of the party horns here!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17231202894687794291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17699701257687718954" style="display:none">Personally, I'm a cat person so if Massie came in My house with that female dog, I would've jumped the girl. <div id="review_65712620" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65712620" />
    <a title="Ashleigh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2578685-ashleigh"><img alt="Ashleigh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425705654p2/2578685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65712620?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleigh" href="/user/show/2578685-ashleigh">Ashleigh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes young adult books with unreasonably rich people and lots of drama.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ashleigh by: </span>
      Discovered on my own.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2578685-ashleigh?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2578685-ashleigh?shelf=two-books-a-week-2009">two-books-a-week-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65712620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5841949208776720805">This is probably one of my favorite Clique books so far. While most of the books had the problem totally resolved in the end (or mostly), this one left it open. Out of all of them, I as most excited to see what happened in the next book after this one. I also like how they used a lot more pop culture references in their similes and metaphors and in general speaking. Overall, it kept my attention, kept my guessing and I really liked it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review65712620">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3650258861?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Opal ...." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Opal ...." href="/user/show/14207667-opal">Opal ....</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3650258861&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3650258861" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12531218932531498554">This by far has been my favourite book of the series Massie coming to terms with maturity, changes in her life and friendships but also realizing how she shouldn’t trap herself in a role or change who she is to keep others around.<br/> Lisa did an incredible job displaying Massie’s change and growth in this book but also keeping her the same melodramatic diva she’s always been “Certain that people who lost their friends were expected to sob uncontrollably and that if she did, the PC would sense her d</span>
  <span id="freeText12531218932531498554" style="display:none">This by far has been my favourite book of the series Massie coming to terms with maturity, changes in her life and friendships but also realizing how she shouldn’t trap herself in a role or change who she is to keep others around.<br /> Lisa did an incredible job displaying Massie’s change and growth in this book but also keeping her the same melodramatic diva she’s always been “Certain that people who lost their friends were expected to sob uncontrollably and that if she did, the PC would sense her despair and stampede toward her with open arms. But no matter how many times she pictured Bean getting hit by an SUV, her eyes refused to cooperate” I laughed out loud and thought that’s Massie that’s exactly who she is and I loved it it shows that although she’s growing and becoming more confident with who she is alone she also has those moments of falling back into her old patterns I’m really interested to see how she handles in the next book and now that the pretty committee has completely foiled down to Claire &amp; Massie how that will change the dynamic going forward - Great read and I can’t wait to burn through the next book of the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12531218932531498554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3851993800529805235">This series inspired a generation of middle school girls to think being mean made you cool, and that lying and scheming were legit social skills. In lockstep with their counterparts (designed for older and hopefully less susceptible audiences) Pretty Little Liars and Gossip Girl, these books glorify being skinny, white, rich, and materialistic by using the most extra and clunky similes and filling space by name-dropping brands.<br/><br/>This book was saved by my main bitch, Layne, who BARFED ON MASSIE on </span>
  <span id="freeText3851993800529805235" style="display:none">This series inspired a generation of middle school girls to think being mean made you cool, and that lying and scheming were legit social skills. In lockstep with their counterparts (designed for older and hopefully less susceptible audiences) Pretty Little Liars and Gossip Girl, these books glorify being skinny, white, rich, and materialistic by using the most extra and clunky similes and filling space by name-dropping brands.<br /><br />This book was saved by my main bitch, Layne, who BARFED ON MASSIE on PURPOSE so she could ride a roller coaster with Dempsey. As a theme park employee, it made my heart sing. Also, the "Are you an X? Then why are you Y?" joke structure deserves an honorable mention. But my anecdotal evidence of the shitty impact of these books will not let me give this one anything above 2 stars. </span>

  <span id="freeText9477839130427766152" style="display:none">This book was good but confusing because of all the love triangles? The alpha of the Pretty Committee is crushing on the same person as an LBR (in other words outsiders). Alicia ended up rebelling and starting her own cheering leading clique with her as the alpha. And to me personally, this book was fairly confusing until three-quarter way through and I am a current a grade 10 (as of the time this post was written and the time this book was read).</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11887451921918736350">AKA, "The Clique 10: In Which Dylan Finally Learns She's the Best Character and Stands Up to Massie"<br/><br/>Have the other girls finally learned their lesson? Will they finally stop compromising their true dreams and their own goals for popularity and Massie's approval? Is Massie turning over a new leaf and learning to accept others for who they are instead of moulding them into who she wants them to be? <br/><br/>...Probably not.</span>

<div id="review_276700509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276700509" />
    <a title="Aditi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7178380-aditi"><img alt="Aditi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328011463p2/7178380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/276700509?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aditi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aditi" href="/user/show/7178380-aditi">Aditi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer276700509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5639721119329592381">The 10th book in the New York Times Best Selling series: ‘The Clique’, P.S I Loathe You by Lisi Harrison is a fictional novel, telling the story of Octavian Country Day’s most popular clique and the drama they experience behind the scenes on an everyday basis. <br/>The Pretty Committee's “Boy fast” has ended and Massie and her posse are back on the prowl. Despite this, and however confident and assured they may seem, complications bubbling under the surface are threatening to explode: Tarnishing the </span>
  <span id="freeText5639721119329592381" style="display:none">The 10th book in the New York Times Best Selling series: ‘The Clique’, P.S I Loathe You by Lisi Harrison is a fictional novel, telling the story of Octavian Country Day’s most popular clique and the drama they experience behind the scenes on an everyday basis. <br />The Pretty Committee's “Boy fast” has ended and Massie and her posse are back on the prowl. Despite this, and however confident and assured they may seem, complications bubbling under the surface are threatening to explode: Tarnishing the girls’ reputations and staining their wardrobes like the pigeons accumulating around the Briarwood boys’ trailers. Both Alpha Massie and Unpopular Layne both have eyes for Dempsey Solomon, and Kristen is caught in the middle, with loyalties to both friends. Will she be able to help out the leaders of the Witty and the Pretty Committee without the other knowing, or will her two worlds collide leaving her painfully alone? And is it truly either of them that Dempsey really wants? Meanwhile, Tomboy redhead Dylan has to harbor a secret crush: Massie’s ex boyfriend Derrick, a secret romance that could end her friendship with Massie forever, but that Dylan just can not ignore. On top of it all, Spanish Beauty Alicia finds herself contemplating her role in the clique, and as the bottom of the pyramid in Massie’s new cheerleading squad, she’s almost reached her limit. As the girl who once started her own clique, is she strong enough to do it again... And maybe this time succeed? Through forbidden romance, crumbling friendships and constant insecurity, the clique will open the door to the secret lives of this Westchester County Clique, and the twisted truth behind their immaculate appearances and ever shiny lip gloss. <br />One of the most memorable scenes in the novel was the scene where Derrick and Dylan wash cars together as a punishment for some school time pranks they pulled. They talk, and Dylan feels a tugging hope that maybe somehow they will be together, but that hope is buried by insecurity and fear. They really get to know each other in this scene, and we see how much Dylan values their relationship through a detailed insight into her mind. We also realize that she is willing to put her friendship with Massie in jeopardy for their relationship and ponder what Derrick’s true motives. <br />Another memorable scene, was the scene where Dune and Layne both find out the secrets Kristen has been hiding from them and storm out of her apartment, leaving her crying on the floor with only her mother to comfort her. It is definitely one of the most dramatic scenes in the novel, and Kristen has been juggling lots of different problems throughout the story, so the moment when they all collide is what it has been leading up to. Dune is angered by the realization that she had lost his token of love, and Layne realizes that she has been trying to fix both her and Massie up with the same boy. They both feel intensely betrayed, and Kristen feels the problems she was balancing crash down around her. <br />The Clique series is one that has always been a favourite of mine, and with it’s vivid descriptions, heated conflict and soap opera worthy drama: It is a read that will keep you easily captivated. I recommend this novel for fans of Lisi Harrison, or similar series like ‘The It Girl Series’ and ‘Pretty Little Liars’, as it will please anyone who enjoys chick literature. The series is targeted for girls from 12 up, and therefore would be the most enjoyable for this age group, but the book is versatile, it simply may not be as well understood, or may seem a bit immature for audiences too young or old. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5639721119329592381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4187729670371125947" style="display:none">	After the Pretty Committee’s boyfast totally failed, they are no BFFWC (BFFs with crushes). Claire is finally secure in her relationship with Cam as is Alicia with Josh. Dylan is C-minus (without a crush), and Massie has an unrequited crush on Dempsey who LBR Layne likes as well. Claire is BFFs with Layne as is Kristen except she keeps their relationship a secret claiming it’s to protect their secret Witty Committee. Kristen finds herself torn as she promised to help both of them get Dempsey. Meanwhile, Dylan has a requited crush on Derrington, Massie’s ex-crush, whom she calls by his real name Derrick, but they must keep their relationship secret as he is still marked by Massie until she releases her hold which she won’t until she gets Dempsey. When Derrick sprains his ankle, Dempsey fills in as soccer captain. To show her support Massie forms a cheerleading squad with the PC and Layne (by request of Dempsey), her friend (guy), and another girl. Kristen’s crush Dune returns, but she finds she doesn’t feel the same way about him and starts crushing on Dempsey though she doesn’t realize it. She pretends to be into Dune still though. Kristen is not on the cheerleading squad as her over-protective mother won’t let her wear the uniform. Alicia conflicts with Massie in that she tries to order the team as she wishes to choreograph the routines and such. When they end up shoving each other, Dempsey gets his ankle fractured. The Cheerleading squad is over and out. Massie finds out about Kristen’s friendship with Layne and that she was helping her with Dempsey as Layne finds out she was helping Massie, too, and that the real reason she wanted to keep their friendship a secret was for Kristen’s own popularity and acceptance. Kristen lied to Dune about not having lost the shark tooth necklace for she did and Layne found it and planned to keep it until Kristen helped her get Dempsey. Dune saw it on Layne’s neck when she stormed out after Massie and he upset by her lying followed suit. Massie goes to Alicia’s to find that she has formed a new cheerleading squad which she is alpha of. She invites Massie, but the betrayal is too much. Dylan and Derrick admit to their relationship to Massie and they get into an argument about Massie holding her friends back and being controlling. Dylan and Derrick want Massie to release Derrick and so she does, but she released Dylan as well. Claire arrives to the PC-less traditional Friday night sleepover with Cam who leaves quickly after as he’s picked up. Claire is the only one there for Massie. Kristen finds out that Dempsey isn’t interested in either Massie or Layne for he likes Kristen and though she doesn’t tell him she feels the same way. Dune is right there having forgiven Kristen and she goes with it though she’s really confused as to what to do now. Massie is prepared to make a new Clique now as the PC besides Massie and Claire are broken up. <br />	There were a string of complications with the boys, competition, and Massie’s control issues. I was surprised Dempsey and Kristen ended up having requited crushes as I am that Dylan and Derrick were matched up too. It was a mesh of emotions and it’s really unfortunate that the PC is broken up right now. <br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4187729670371125947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69058655" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69058655" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69058655?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69058655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8984608667520993405">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>The Pretty Committee is back, and they are far from love and friendship. In fact, it seems like the more and more they are together, the more they just can't stand each other.<br/><br/>The only thing that is more unstable than their friendship are the boys in their lives.<br/><br/>To cut it short, Massie has moved on to another soccer player, Dempsey, who just so happens to be great friends with Layne. Even though Massie says she's over Derrington</span>
  <span id="freeText8984608667520993405" style="display:none">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />The Pretty Committee is back, and they are far from love and friendship. In fact, it seems like the more and more they are together, the more they just can't stand each other.<br /><br />The only thing that is more unstable than their friendship are the boys in their lives.<br /><br />To cut it short, Massie has moved on to another soccer player, Dempsey, who just so happens to be great friends with Layne. Even though Massie says she's over Derrington, Dylan knows if she tells Massie she has a crush on him, things won't bode well for her.<br /><br />Kristen finally has the guy she's literally been waiting for but just isn't sure if he is the right person. Claire seems to be the only one without boy trouble, as she finally has Cam back in her life. The only thing on Alicia's mind is deciding whether she should stick around and take Massie's controlling nature or move on to bigger and better friends.<br /><br />Once again, it seems like the PC are on the brink of breaking up, and the consistency of Massie's overly-boy-loving, bossy self does not help at all. The only character in the entire novel who seems interested in keeping the girls together is Claire.<br /><br />In this installment, Harrison allows readers to get to know Kristen and Dylan more as they are the main narrators. Kristen seems to have it rougher than the other girls, not just because of how her boy just might not be the right one, but also her friendship with Layne is totally forbidden if Massie ever discovered it. Of course, Layne is a better and loyal friend than Massie, but Kristen just isn't sure if she is able to leave the PC behind. Dylan, on the other hand, understands that it would be the ultimate betrayal to date one of her friend's boys, and Massie is no exception.<br /><br />Will Kristen, Dylan, and Alicia finally reach a decision that life would be better off without the ringleader to bark orders, or will they be unable to end the friendship that has lasted between them and Massie for so long?<br /><br />P.S. I LOATHE YOU contains all of the same elements as the other CLIQUE novels: betrayal, gossip, and boys. Fans will not be disappointed in this installment, as they are able to understand Kristen and Dylan more, who were only minor characters in the past.</span>

          </span>

    if (checked && exclusive) {

      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ivDecm9sw+2c8uuZYf9bbZhEAKPJ8xEAwLYKXjXk5DiZxuktMt4QoIe3/PAC61+lzNzVjNi6Rl/ArOa0maXbdg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Zrao5h9b+3oiJHsMlqoWlincVbzuICMPOqovvZ1/IhB1gJ+5QukoNzlhbGX1vhJefUSAk/9pdFA6sMNXMT4dXg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5079942721051799426"><i>Lisi Harrison</i> is the author of the #1 New York Times best-selling series "The Clique", "Alphas", "Monster High," Pretenders," and her first adult novel: "The Dirty Book Club" out 10.10.17. Lisi was born in Toronto, Canada, and lived in NYC for 15 years while she worked at MTV. She now lives in Laguna Beach, CA and is a member or her own Dirty Book Club. <br/><br/><br/><br/></span>
